# Decision journal (append-only)

**Purpose:** Capture **every material decision** as we go—yours, mine (assistant), and the team’s—so we can **audit and backtrack** quickly if something goes wrong. This is a **running log**, not a substitute for ADR-lite files for big boundaries (those stay as `YYYYMMDD-topic.md` and get a one-line pointer here).

**Rules**

1. **Append only** — never delete or rewrite past entries; if we reverse course, add a **new** entry that references the old one (`Supersedes: JE-…`).
2. **Immediate** — log the decision in the same push or the next push when the work lands (same day when possible).
3. **IDs** — each entry gets `JE-YYYY-MM-DD-n` (n = sequence that day) for easy reference in commits and incidents.
4. **Who** — `Anton` | `Assistant (Cursor)` | `Team` | `Vendor` with name if relevant.
5. **Reversibility** — one line: how to undo (env var, revert commit SHA, GitHub toggle).

**How assistants use this file:** After substantive choices in chat or in code, **add a journal row** (and an ADR when the decision changes trust, tenancy, or security).

`User Provided Custom Data Template was successfully rendered` confirms successful template processing). **Fix is persistent**: both bind-mounts live in the Compose override file — survives container recreation (`docker compose up -d`), image upgrade (`docker compose pull && up -d`), and `--force-recreate`. No runtime-symlink dependency. The v1 fix attempt (single bind-mount + symlink-from-backend) had surfaced an unexpected finding — `corpflowai-production_sites` is nominally a shared Docker volume between `backend` and `frontend` per `docker inspect --format '{{ .Mounts }}'`, but in practice the `sites/assets/` subpath behaves as if it is NOT shared (a symlink created via `docker compose exec backend ln -sfn ...` succeeded with exit 0 then `docker compose exec frontend ls ...` returned `No such file or directory` seconds later; backend's `sites/assets/.` `mtime` was `05:33` matching the symlink creation, frontend's was `May 29 12:18` matching original image build; `assets.json` file sizes were 3796 bytes vs 3508 bytes confirming genuinely different directories). Likely root cause is the frappe-docker frontend image's entrypoint copying its baked-in `sites/assets/` over the volume mount on startup, masking it for that subpath specifically. Not investigated further beyond what was needed to ship the editor fix; documented in runbook v2 § 9 as a frappe-docker volume-overlay quirk; pattern of dual bind-mount (`apps/<app>` + `sites/assets/<app>`) is the standard fix for any future Frappe app installed via the bind-mount install pattern whose assets must be served by nginx. **Runbook v2 amendments to `docs/runbooks/ERPNEXT_PRINT_DESIGNER_EDITOR_FIX_PACKET_V1.md`** (committed by THIS PR alongside this JE row): § 2.2 final paragraph rewritten — removed the incorrect "the `sites/` volume is shared with the `frontend` container" assertion + added the executed-evidence finding; § 2.3 fix description updated from v1 "add bind-mount for `apps/print_designer/`" (single-mount) to v2 "add TWO bind-mounts: `apps/print_designer/` AND `sites/assets/print_designer/`" (dual-mount — bypasses volume layer for the asset path); § 4 operator-paste block replaced with the final dual-bind-mount version + Step 7 added curl test for HTTP 200; § 9 added top-bullet documenting the frappe-docker volume-overlay quirk + implication for any future bind-mounted Frappe app whose assets must be served by nginx; § 12 verdict updated to record FIX-PASS at 2026-06-05 05:51 UTC with EV-1..EV-3 evidence + install verdict flip `JE-2026-06-05-4` PARTIAL → PASS recorded under THIS row; § 13 change log v2 entry. Browser-DevTools symptom captured 2026-06-05: `GET /assets/print_designer/dist/js/print_designer.bundle.UDIPLQSC.js → 404 (Not Found)` + `Uncaught SyntaxError: Failed to execute 'appendChild' on 'Node': Unexpected token '<'` (browser parses 404 HTML as JS) + `Uncaught (in promise) TypeError: frappe.ui.PrintDesigner is not a constructor at load_print_designer (print_designer.js:181:28)`. Root cause: the bind-mount Compose override `~/erpnext-production/frappe_docker/overrides/compose.print-designer-mount.yaml` authored during the `JE-2026-06-05-3`-closing install session (and applied via `bench install-app` + `bench build` per `JE-2026-06-05-4` § 2.6) mounts the host-cloned `print_designer/` source into **5 Python services** that need to `import print_designer` at runtime (`backend` + `scheduler` + `queue-short` + `queue-long` + `websocket`) but **not into the `frontend` (nginx) container** — which is the one that serves `/assets/print_designer/dist/...` static bundles. `bench build` writes compiled JS / CSS to `apps/print_designer/print_designer/public/dist/` on the bind-mounted source and symlinks `sites/assets/print_designer/` → `apps/print_designer/print_designer/public/` with an **absolute** target path; when nginx in the frontend container resolves the symlink it follows the absolute path to a location that exists only in the backend container's filesystem view, returns 404, the browser executes the 404 HTML as JS, the `frappe.ui.PrintDesigner` class never registers, the canvas stays blank. | JE-2026-06-01-5 | 2026-06-01 | Anton + Assistant (Cursor) | **ERPNext C-1 final remediation = Option B (custom `Accountant Read-Only` Role with explicit Custom DocPerm rows).** Supersedes the intermediate Auditor-swap remediation step recorded in `JE-2026-06-01-3` finding C-1 and STATUS-11 ([issuecomment-4590998627](https://github.com/antonvdberg-bit/corpflow-ai-command-center/issues/249#issuecomment-4590998627)). **Anton's DECISION ([chat 2026-06-01, "Re: C-1 remediation result — choose Option B"](https://github.com/antonvdberg-bit/corpflow-ai-command-center/issues/249))** rejected Option A (accept Auditor as-is with GL-only read) because Auditor's default DocPerm matrix is too restrictive for practical accountant review — it cannot read Sales Invoice, Payment Entry, Customer, or Item. **Option B scope (sandbox-only, executed):** create a custom Role named `Accountant Read-Only` (`desk_access=1`, `is_custom=1`); prefer changes in `lib/analytics/` + `pages/_document.js`; keep `lib/analytics/` as the single source of truth; preserve SSG for `/lead-rescue`; do not switch `/lead-rescue` to `getServerSideProps`; do not add a page-specific `useEffect` Plausible loader (Option A) unless Option C proves impossible; no new analytics vendors; no PII; no Lead Rescue copy / pricing / layout / form fields / video / payment posture / ERPNext changes; no new env var names; preserve denies; preserve kill-switch. **Why Option A was not chosen:** a page-level `useEffect` loader would solve `/lead-rescue` only and duplicates the deny-list policy in component-side JS — that contradicts the "single source of truth" rule. Option C solves the gap at the analytics-module layer for the whole codebase. **Why Option B was not chosen:** switching `/lead-rescue` from `getStaticProps` to `getServerSideProps` loses static edge caching and is a rendering-mode change with broader implications; not necessary when a smaller fix exists. **Implementation (3 source files, +312 net):** § A `lib/analytics/index.js` (+205 lines): (1) new internal helper `isPathAllowedWithoutHost(fullPath)` that applies the host-independent subset of deny rules — `DENY_PATH_PREFIXES` (word-boundary semantics matching `pathMatchesWordBoundary`), `DENY_PATH_SUBSTRINGS` (reset-password / forgot-password), `DENY_QUERY_KEYS` (token / reset / ticket) — skipping `APEX_DENY_PATH_PREFIXES` because the runtime loader re-applies them once the real host is known; (2) `resolveAnalyticsForRequest` extended to return a new `requiresRuntimeHostCheck` boolean — `false` for the existing SSR path (host known, deny-list applied at SSR time, static `<script>` tag still emitted, Plausible's "Verify your installation" probe still works on apex `/`), `true` for SSG / static-prerender when host is empty AND the path passes every host-independent deny (kill-switch off OR a host-independent path deny still returns `enabled: false` + `requiresRuntimeHostCheck: false` so the loader script is never emitted for paths that can never be allowed at runtime); (3) new export `buildSsgRuntimeLoaderScript({ src, domain })` that returns a self-contained inline JavaScript string (IE11-safe vanilla JS, no module syntax, no external dependencies) which the Document component embeds via `<script dangerouslySetInnerHTML>` — the script reads `window.location.hostname` + `pathname` + `search` and re-applies the EXACT SAME deny logic against policy data serialised inline at build time from `lib/analytics/config.js` (allow list, host-exact + host-suffix denies, path-prefix denies with word-boundary, apex-specific denies that only apply when host equals `APEX_HOST`, path substring denies, query-key denies), and only when ALL checks pass does it dynamically `document.createElement('script')` and append the Plausible tag to `<head>`; the entire body is wrapped in `try { … } catch (e) {}` so a runtime error inside the policy check never breaks the host page. § B `pages/_document.js` (+24 lines): import `buildSsgRuntimeLoaderScript`; render branch — when `analytics.requiresRuntimeHostCheck` is true, emit the inline loader via `dangerouslySetInnerHTML`; else emit the canonical static `<script defer data-domain=… src=…>` tag as before; updated the JSDoc preamble to describe the two render strategies (SSR static tag + SSG runtime-host-gated loader) and to note the multi-host SSG-output reality (Lux + Core + preview all serve the same prerendered HTML on `/lead-rescue` — verified live during PR #291 DRA preparation — which is why the runtime check is required). § C `node-tests/analytics-policy.test.mjs` (+205 lines, +20 new tests, 1 existing test updated to reflect new behaviour): 7 tests pinning `resolveAnalyticsForRequest` new contract (SSR apex unchanged; SSG fallback respects kill-switch off in `false` / `''` / `undefined` states; SSG fallback enables for `null` / `undefined` / `''` / `'   '` hosts; SSG fallback with env overrides returns the overridden domain/src), plus 12 tests executing the loader inside a Node `vm.createContext` sandbox with a mocked `window.location` + `document.createElement` + `document.head.appendChild`: empty-input guard returns empty string; The loader's first check is `denyExact.indexOf(h) !== -1` followed by `denySuffix` iteration; only after those host-deny checks pass does it test `allow.indexOf(h) !== -1`. Result: Lux / Core / `*.vercel.app` previews / `localhost` all hit the loader, all read `window.location.hostname`, all fail the allow check, all `return` without injecting Plausible. Approved scope: minimal runtime change following the existing `lib/analytics/` pattern (single source of truth for analytics policy + helpers); no backend changes; no new env var names; no payment changes; no ERPNext changes; no Pomelli activation; no copy changes in this PR. **Four events** (lowercased snake_case, plain-text event names matching Anton's authorisation wording verbatim): (1) **`lr_primary_cta_click`** with optional `props.location` string (`'nav'` or `'hero'`) — fires on click of the nav `Start the 48-hour setup` anchor (`components/AiLeadRescueLanding.js` ~line 215) and on click of the hero `Start my 48-hour setup` anchor (~line 226), neither call prevents default anchor navigation to `#intake`; (2) **`lr_secondary_cta_click`** (no props) — fires on click of the hero `See how it works` anchor (~line 227) navigating to `#how-it-works`; (3) **`lr_intake_submit_attempt`** (no props) — fires at the very top of `submitLead(e)` after `e.preventDefault()`, before `FormData` extraction and before `fetch('/api/tenant/intake', ...)`; (4) **`lr_intake_submit_success`** (no props) — fires after `if (!r.ok) throw new Error('intake_failed')` passes, before the success `alert(...)` and before `form.reset()`. **Implementation pattern** — new exported helper **`trackEvent(eventName, options)`** in `lib/analytics/index.js` (single source of truth for analytics — same module that already exports `resolveAnalyticsForRequest` for SSR Plausible script injection in `pages/_document.js`). The helper short-circuits silently and returns `false` when (a) `eventName` is not a non-empty string, (b) `typeof window === 'undefined'` (SSR), (c) `typeof window.plausible !== 'function'` (script not injected — kill-switch off, host on the deny list, preview deploy, network failure), or (d) Plausible itself throws inside the try/catch wrapper. Returns `true` only when the call dispatched. No additional host/path check is needed inside the helper because policy enforcement happens upstream in `_document.js` via `resolveAnalyticsForRequest` — if the script tag was never injected, `window.plausible` is undefined and the helper no-ops. **No-PII rule** — call sites in `components/AiLeadRescueLanding.js` pass only the event name and at most a single small categorical `props.location` value (`'nav'` or `'hero'`) — never email / name / phone / business name / IP / fingerprint / user-id / session-id / form field values. The helper itself does not enforce shape; call-site discipline does, documented in the `trackEvent` JSDoc and protected by the new `trackEvent never carries PII` unit test which validates the lowercased snake_case event-name regex + the location-value whitelist + the forbidden-prop-key blocklist (`email` / `name` / `phone` / `ip` / `fingerprint` / `user_id` / `session_id`). **Form behaviour preserved** — `submitLead` is unchanged structurally: `e.preventDefault()` still fires first; `FormData` extraction unchanged; `fetch('/api/tenant/intake', ...)` body unchanged; `!r.ok` failure path unchanged (alert + early return); success path unchanged (success alert + `form.reset()`); error path unchanged (catch alert). The two `trackEvent` calls inside `submitLead` are fire-and-forget — they never throw (try/catch internal), never `await`, never block the network call, and never reach the catch block of the calling function. Form submission works identically whether the Plausible script is loaded or absent. **Files changed** — **3 files** (small, surgical): `lib/analytics/index.js` (+58 lines — new `trackEvent` export with JSDoc); `components/AiLeadRescueLanding.js` (+13 lines net — new import line + 2 `trackEvent` calls in `submitLead` + 3 `onClick={() => trackEvent(...)}` props on existing anchors, no markup or copy changed otherwise); `node-tests/analytics-policy.test.mjs` (+118 lines — 7 new tests: SSR no-op / script-not-injected no-op / invalid event names rejected / plain-event dispatch / options-with-props dispatch / Plausible-throws caught silently / no-PII whitelist + regex shape validation). **Verification** — `npm test` `428/428` pass (was `421/421` before this PR; +7 tests added by this packet; no existing test changed); `npm run build` succeeds (`/lead-rescue` SSG built at 539ms with no warnings); `npm run check:marketing-quality-gate` PASS (all 6 marketing doctrine docs present + marker terms intact). **Live measurement plan** — once merged + Vercel Production deploy is `READY`, Anton confirms in Plausible dashboard (apex site `corpflowai.com`) that the 4 events appear as Custom Events / Goals over the next 24-48 hours of organic traffic. If a cold outreach campaign starts before that confirmation, Anton has the option to use the absence of events to prove the dashboard wiring rather than the absence of clicks. **Hard limits honoured:** zero backend changes (no `lib/server/*` / no `api/*` / no `prisma/*` / no DB schema / no migration); zero new env var names introduced (the existing `NEXT_PUBLIC_PLAUSIBLE_ENABLED` / `NEXT_PUBLIC_PLAUSIBLE_DOMAIN` / `NEXT_PUBLIC_PLAUSIBLE_SRC` continue to govern script injection); zero payment changes (no `pages/refund-policy.js` / `pages/terms.js` / `pages/contact.js` / `components/PublicSiteFooter.js` / `LR-Pay-1` wording / `PAY-SBM-2` copy / pricing / forbidden-phrase exposure touched); zero ERPNext changes (no sandbox state / Phase D / Phase C² / runbook §8.1 / production instance / scheduler / accountant work touched); zero Pomelli activation (no Google account / VPN / asset upload / first-asset trial run / personal-data exposure); zero copy changes (no headline / sub-headline / body / CTA wording / form labels / error messages / privacy / refund / terms / contact / footer / hero-trust-band SVG / walkthrough video / asset manifest touched); zero secrets / API keys / OAuth tokens / DB credentials / banking details / KYC material / signed documents / DNS / mail-routing / Vercel config / GitHub Secrets / GitHub workflow files / Telegram / Search Console / payment-settings / payment-automation / CRM-GHL-WhatsApp-SMS integration touched; zero Lux tenant / `lux.corpflowai.com` / `core.corpflowai.com` / factory / operator-console / `/change` / `/admin` route touched (Plausible policy already excludes them — they remain excluded). | JE-2026-06-04-2 | 2026-06-04 | Anton + Assistant (Cursor) | **Server agent access & execution boundary v1 — canonical (docs-only).** New canonical doc **`docs/operations/SERVER_AGENT_ACCESS_AND_EXECUTION_BOUNDARY_V1.md`** (anchor sentinel `<!-- SERVER_AGENT_ACCESS_AND_EXECUTION_BOUNDARY_V1 -->`) names the three execution layers that exist in CorpFlow today — **L1 laptop brain** (Cursor on Anton's machine; authors / captures), **L2 cloud hands** (Vercel HTTP routes + cron, GitHub Actions, Postgres / Neon, n8n, Codex Cloud — all deterministic / secret-protected / 24/7), **L3 box hands** (operator-driven SSH from Anton's terminal to `corpflow-exec-01-u69678`, where Anton pastes commands authored by Cursor on L1). § 5.4 codifies the proven **Phase B-a collaboration pattern** used by `JE-2026-05-31-2` + `JE-2026-06-01-1`: Cursor (L1) drafts the exact command block in a docs-only runbook; Anton opens his own SSH session on L3 and pastes; Anton shares output back in chat; Cursor (L1) captures into JE row + bridge [#249](https://github.com/antonvdberg-bit/corpflow-ai-command-center/issues/249) STATUS; Cursor (L1) opens a docs-only PR. § 6 records the **canonical-absence list** of surfaces that do **NOT** exist on the box (Cursor session on the box · Cursor Remote SSH endpoint to the box · `code-server` / VS Code Server on the box · web-shell / browser terminal on the box · persistent daemon / systemd / cron / `at` on the box · Codex Cloud on the box · Tailscale / WireGuard / reverse-tunnel from box to laptop · production secrets on the box · Vercel deploy from the box · tenant DB exports on the box · n8n on the box) and the rule: *"if an agent or handoff comment claims one of these surfaces exists, demand the file path / process / port / config row that proves it; if none can be produced, the claim is wrong."* § 7 formalises `HOST_MISMATCH` semantics: when an L1 session detects (a) the packet authorisation row requires execution on `corpflow-exec-01-u69678`, (b) the current session is not running on that host, and (c) the packet requires bytes to change on L3, the session must stop immediately, post evidence to bridge #249 naming why L3 is unreachable from the current host, and hand off to Anton + L1 in the § 5.4 pattern — never fabricate L3 output, never proceed silently. § 8 provides the per-class **decision tree** (docs-only edit → L1; scheduled/event-driven repo automation → L2; DB writes → L2 via audited API route; one-off shell command on the box → L3 via § 5.4 pattern; "Cursor on the box itself" → does not exist as a class). § 9 enumerates the **anti-patterns** including the **2026-06-04 handoff mistake** that triggered this runbook ([#249 issuecomment-4617719340](https://github.com/antonvdberg-bit/corpflow-ai-command-center/issues/249#issuecomment-4617719340) claimed *"resume in a Cursor instance running on `corpflow-exec-01-u69678` itself (same posture as Phase B-a sandbox install)"* — both clauses factually wrong; no such Cursor instance has ever existed, and Phase B-a was Anton-at-keyboard pasting laptop-Cursor-authored commands). § 10 names the **gate for lifting any § 5.3 hard rule** (e.g. installing Cursor Remote SSH on the box, scheduling `exec01-cron-pulse`, migrating n8n to `corpflow-exec-01`): an ADR under `docs/decisions/YYYYMMDD-<topic>.md` + `MIGRATION_TO_SERVER_CHECKLIST.md` § 2 pass + new row in `MONITORING_ARCHITECTURE.md` § 2 + update to this runbook moving the surface from § 6 absence to § 5 allowed + new `AGENTS.md` Must-read row + new `JE-YYYY-MM-DD-N` row + Anton merge approval. § 11 cross-references all source-of-truth docs the runbook synthesises (`EXECUTION_BRAIN_VS_HANDS.md`, `MONITORING_ARCHITECTURE.md` § 11.3, `DELIVERY_ACCELERATION_V1.md` § 4.3, `MIGRATION_TO_SERVER_CHECKLIST.md`, `CORPFLOW_AUTONOMOUS_ACTIONS_POLICY.md`, `CORPFLOW_EXECUTION_PACKET_STANDARD.md`, `CODEX_CLOUD_INSTALL.md`, `ERPNEXT_SANDBOX_INSTALL.md` § 10, `SECURITY_OR_INCIDENT.md`, `CORPFLOW_COMMUNICATIONS_V1.md`, `POSTGRES_PROVIDER.md`, `OPERATOR_BRIDGE_V1.md`, decision rows `JE-2026-05-29-1` / `JE-2026-05-29-2` / `JE-2026-05-31-2` / `JE-2026-06-01-1` / `JE-2026-06-01-3` / `JE-2026-06-01-5` / `JE-2026-06-03-2` / `JE-2026-06-03-3` / `JE-2026-06-04-1` / this row). § 13 change log marks v1. **`AGENTS.md` Must-read row added** in the same PR (immediately below the `MONITORING_ARCHITECTURE.md` row) so future agents discover this runbook on every cold-read. **Authorisation provenance:** Anton's APPROVED investigation directive on bridge [#249 issuecomment-4617928519](https://github.com/antonvdberg-bit/corpflow-ai-command-center/issues/249#issuecomment-4617928519) (2026-06-04 *"Operator / ChatGPT decision — investigate server-side Cursor/agent execution reality"*) + Anton's structured decision via `AskQuestion` (2026-06-04 *Q1 = Option B "proven Phase B-a model"*; | JE-2026-06-04-4 | 2026-06-04 | Anton + Assistant (Cursor) | **ERPNext Print Designer evaluation v1 — DECISION RECORDED (docs-only research; no installation; no production-shell mutation).** New canonical doc **`docs/finance/ERPNEXT_PRINT_DESIGNER_EVALUATION_V1.md`** (anchor sentinel `<!-- ERPNEXT_PRINT_DESIGNER_EVALUATION_V1 -->`) records the outcome of Anton's chat DECISION (2026-06-04 *"AUTHORISE — ERPNext-Print-Designer-Evaluation-1"*). Anton attempted manual ERPNext classic Letter Head / Print Format editing on `corpflowai-production.localhost` and hit four symptoms (image scaling unreliable, script/comment text appearing in printed output, `wkhtmltopdf ConnectionRefusedError`, manual UI editing too error-prone); evaluation packet directed Cursor to research whether Frappe Print Designer or a similar PDF/document design system should replace classic Letter Head / Print Format for CorpFlowAI client-facing ERPNext documents. **Five live sources consulted (2026-06-04):** S1 `frappe/print_designer` GitHub repo + `README.md` (confirmed v15 compatibility — README warning *"only compatible with develop and V15 version of frappe framework"*; stable v1.6.7 released 2026-02-10; 421 GitHub stars; official Frappe-team-owned); S2 Print Designer install guides (`techsolvo.com` + YouTube walkthrough — standard install `bench get-app` + `install-app` + `bench build` + `bench migrate`, installs into existing site); S3 `frappe/print_designer` PR #399 *"feat: Chrome PDF Generator"* (Chromium-based PDF backend alternative to wkhtmltopdf: **2.21–2.79× faster**, **2.27–2.73× lower CPU**, toggleable per Print Format via `pdf_generator` field, Frappe Cloud explicitly *"not supported for now"* for Chrome backend); S4 `frappe/frappe` PR #35812 + Issue #35546 (Chrome backend upstreamed into Frappe core for v16; v15 has it via Print Designer + Print Settings; v16 still downloads Chromium into bench dir rather than using OS package — production should install `chromium-headless-shell` as a system package + set `chromium_binary_path` in `common_site_config.json`); S5 `frappe/erpnext` Issue #36018 + `frappe/frappe_docker` Issue #1589 + Aakvatech *"Fix ERPNext PDF Letterhead Issues"* (the `wkhtmltopdf ConnectionRefusedError` is a Frappe-Docker `host_name` mismatch — backend container cannot resolve site's loopback hostname; fix: set `host_name` to a URL the backend container can reach internally, typically `http://frontend:8080`; wkhtmltopdf upstream archived 2023, abandoned). **Diagnosis of in-flight symptoms:** (i) `ConnectionRefusedError` is a Docker `host_name` issue, NOT a Letter Head problem; (ii) image scaling unreliable because wkhtmltopdf's QtWebKit fork doesn't honour modern CSS sizing; (iii) script/comment text appearing because Letter Head `Source` dropdown was left on `HTML` while raw text or comment markers were pasted; (iv) manual UI too error-prone because the classic editor is what Frappe themselves built Print Designer to replace ("can take days or weeks" for non-trivial formats per README). **Verdict matrix (recorded in § 4 of the new doc):** **A** (install Print Designer into existing production shell) = **EVALUATE-SEPARATELY → recommend GO via a new authorisation packet** (best-fit for v15; reversible; resolves renderer-quality problem long-term); **B** (separate self-hosted site) = **NO-GO** (loses access to live doctype data); **C** (Frappe Cloud + Print Designer) = **NO-GO for v1** (contradicts `JE-2026-05-29-1` self-hosted decision; Chrome backend *"FC not supported"*; new paid vendor); **D** (build own PDF renderer) = **NO-GO** (duplicates ERPNext data model + audit trail; high maintenance debt); **E** (continue classic Letter Head) = **NO-GO for v1.5+ / TRANSITIONAL-only** (wkhtmltopdf abandoned; emergency single-PDF use acceptable if `host_name` is fixed first). **Two future-packet shapes defined (NOT authorised by this JE row):** Packet 1 `ERPNext-Production-Shell-host_name-Fix-1` (~10 min L3 work — discovery + set-config + clear-cache + minimal smoke + sandbox preservation re-check); Packet 2 `ERPNext-PrintDesigner-Install-1` (~3 hours L3 work + ~60 min design — install Print Designer v1.6.7 + Chrome backend + template work); each requires its own separate `AUTHORISE — …` chat DECISION. **Adjacent docs-only files updated:** `AGENTS.md` Must-read row added immediately below the `ERPNEXT_PRODUCTION_SHELL_SETUP_RECIPE.md` row from `JE-2026-06-04-3` so future agents discover the eval on cold-read; `artifacts/chat_history.md` dated section for human continuity. **Hard limits honoured by THIS PR (the evaluation doc + closure JE rows only):** zero installation of Print Designer; zero ERPNext production-shell mutation; zero ERPNext sandbox mutation; zero SSH commands; zero secrets touched; zero edits to `api/` / `lib/` / `components/` / `pages/` / `prisma/` / `middleware*` / `scripts/` / `public/` / `core/engine/` / `.env*` / `.github/` / `vercel.json` / `next.config*` / `package*.json` / `tsconfig*`; `wkhtmltopdf --version` returns `0.12.6.1 (with patched qt)` — the correct patched version inside the backend container, so the renderer engine itself was fine; current `host_name` value was **unset** in `sites/corpflowai-production.localhost/site_config.json` (confirmed root cause of the `ConnectionRefusedError`); ERPNext production-shell doctype inventory: one Letter Head `CorpFlowAI Letterhead` exists (operator-created manually, named differently from recipe § 9's `CorpFlowAI Ltd - Production Letter Head`); zero `CFLR-` prefixed Print Formats; no test customer `Test Buyer (CFLR-DRY-RUN)`; no Item `LR-SETUP-USD-150` — recipe § 11 / § 13 / § 15 / § 16 were never run because Anton went into the UI after recipe § 7 wizard bypass and attempted manual Letter Head work directly. **Recipe latent bug discovered:** Block A's Quotation query failed with `pymysql.err.OperationalError: (1054, "Unknown column 'remarks' in 'SELECT'")` because v15 Quotation doctype has `customer_remarks` (Text Long), not `remarks`; recipe § 16 idempotency check uses `remarks` and will need to be fixed to `customer_remarks` in a separate small follow-up recipe-correction PR. **What changed (Block B execution, 2026-06-04 ~11:03 UTC+4):** (1) `docker compose -p corpflowai-production exec -T backend bench --site corpflowai-production.localhost set-config host_name "http://frontend:8080"` — wrote `host_name` key to `site_config.json`. (2) `bench --site corpflowai-production.localhost clear-cache` — cleared Frappe app cache so the new value is picked up on next request. (3) Minimal raw-HTML PDF smoke via `frappe.utils.pdf.get_pdf()` against a 6-line inline HTML string (no doctype dependencies, no Item/Customer/Quotation/Letter Head touched — zero blast radius) — rendered successfully to `/tmp/host_name_fix_smoke.pdf` inside the backend container. (4) `docker compose -p corpflowai-production cp backend:/tmp/host_name_fix_smoke.pdf ~/host_name_fix_smoke.pdf` — copied PDF out to host filesystem so Anton can `scp` to laptop for visual review. **Root cause confirmed:** `host_name` was unset in `sites/corpflowai-production.localhost/site_config.json`. With `host_name` unset, Frappe's PDF wrapper passes the site's loopback hostname (`corpflowai-production.localhost`) to wkhtmltopdf as the asset-fetch base URL. The backend container cannot resolve `corpflowai-production.localhost` (only the host machine's `/etc/hosts` resolves loopback aliases; Docker DNS resolves Compose service names like `frontend`, `db`, etc.), so wkhtmltopdf hits `ConnectionRefusedError` when fetching its own asset URLs (CSS, fonts, dynamic content). Setting `host_name` to `http://frontend:8080` resolves through Docker DNS to the frontend container, which proxies back to the backend; wkhtmltopdf successfully fetches assets and completes the render. **Verification:** (a) `frappe.utils.get_url()` returns `http://frontend:8080` (Frappe-level confirmation that the new value is being read); (b) `frappe.conf.get('host_name')` returns `http://frontend:8080` (direct site-config read confirms the value is persisted); (c) PDF magic bytes = `25504446` (= `%PDF`, valid PDF document); (d) PDF size = 18,108 bytes (~18 KB, normal for the minimal HTML); (e) `SMOKE_VERDICT: PASS` from the Block B Python orchestrator; (f) PDF on host filesystem at `/home/anton/host_name_fix_smoke.pdf` (`-rw-r--r-- 1 anton anton 18108 Jun 4 07:03`); (g) `docker compose ls` post-fix shows BOTH `corpflowai-production` AND `corpflowai-sandbox` as `running(9)` — sandbox preservation confirmed. **Visual review:** PDF is a minimal text-only document (no Letter Head, no Item, no Quotation data); operator can `scp anton@5.78.213.185:~/host_name_fix_smoke.pdf ~/Downloads/` and open locally; expected content is a `<h1>CorpFlowAI host_name fix smoke test</h1>` heading + 3 lines of body text + a smoke sentinel `HOST_NAME_FIX_SMOKE_OK`. **Hard limits honoured by THIS execution (Packet 1):** loopback only (no public exposure of the production shell — site remains bound to `127.0.0.1:8081` on the host); no DNS / TLS / SMTP changes; no Sales Invoice created or submitted; no GL entry posted; no VAT activated; no real bank / SWIFT / IBAN / BIC / routing / sort-code / card / payment-gateway credentials entered; no Print Designer installed (deferred to Packet 2); no scheduler / queue worker container restart (deferred — interactive PDF render works fine without; email-attachment PDFs rendered in worker processes may need restart to pick up new `host_name` value, recommended in the next operational cycle); no real client invoice / pro-forma issued or emailed; no secrets printed (only file paths, sizes, magic bytes, and Frappe-API readback of the new `host_name` value reported); zero CorpFlowAI runtime / Vercel / GitHub workflows / Postgres / Neon / Prisma / n8n / Plausible / Telegram / Search Console / payment-settings / public-surface mutations; zero ERPNext sandbox mutation (project `corpflowai-sandbox`, site `corpflowai-sandbox.localhost`, credentials file `~/.erpnext-sandbox-credentials` all untouched). **Verdict per `.cursor/rules/delivery-reality.mdc` § operational completion (4-state model):** **state 4 — Live verified** for the *host_name fix* (set-config persisted + readback confirmed + PDF smoke PASS on the actual production-shell site `corpflowai-production.localhost` on `corpflow-exec-01-u69678`). The previous `wkhtmltopdf ConnectionRefusedError` is resolved; recipe § 16-style PDF rendering is now structurally unblocked. **Standing holds (unchanged by this row):** all holds enumerated in `JE-2026-06-04-3` § *Standing holds*; this fix does NOT close HB-2 / HB-3 / HB-4 / Phase D go-live / first submitted Sales Invoice / first ERPNext-emailed PDF to a real client / sandbox tear-down four-condition gate. The Print Designer Packet 2 from `JE-2026-06-04-4` § 7.2 (full Print Designer install + Chrome PDF backend + template work) remains UNAUTHORISED and HELD pending a separate `AUTHORISE — ERPNext-PrintDesigner-Install-1` chat DECISION from Anton. **New holds introduced by this row:** none. **Follow-up work identified during this execution (separate small PRs, not authorised by this row):** (i) recipe-vs-reality doc-drift fix in `ERPNEXT_PRODUCTION_SHELL_SETUP_RECIPE.md` § 5 — update Docker project names from `erpnext-production` / `erpnext-sandbox` to `corpflowai-production` / `corpflowai-sandbox` to match the operator-deployed reality; (ii) recipe latent-bug fix in `ERPNEXT_PRODUCTION_SHELL_SETUP_RECIPE.md` § 16 — change `remarks` to `customer_remarks` in the idempotency check (Quotation v15 schema); (iii) recipe `compose.cf-production-port.yaml` override-file name in § 5 — operator-deployed reality uses `compose.corpflowai-production-noproxy.yaml`; recipe should mention either path is acceptable or align on one; (iv) operator UI cleanup — Anton's existing manually-created `CorpFlowAI Letterhead` Letter Head may have script-bleed-through text from the failed manual editing attempts; visual review recommended, and either repair the existing Letter Head or replace it with the text-only one from recipe § 9 before any real pro-forma rendering; (v) scheduler / queue worker container restart — recommended in the next operational cycle so background-rendered PDFs (e.g., email attachments) pick up the new `host_name` value (interactive PDF renders already work without restart). **None of (i)–(v) are blockers for the COMPLETE verdict on this row** — they are post-closure quality improvements that ride on the cleared rendering path. | Revoking the host_name fix: `docker compose -p corpflowai-production exec -T backend bench --site corpflowai-production.localhost set-config host_name ""` (sets the value to empty string, reverting to the pre-fix unset state — wkhtmltopdf would once again hit `ConnectionRefusedError`); follow with `bench --site corpflowai-production.localhost clear-cache`. | JE-2026-06-04-6 | 2026-06-04 | Anton + Assistant (Cursor) | **`ERPNext-Production-Shell-Recipe-Drift-Fix-1` — `ERPNEXT_PRODUCTION_SHELL_SETUP_RECIPE.md` v1.1 drift fix (docs-only; no host commands; no ERPNext mutation; no runtime changes).** Anton's chat DECISION (2026-06-04 *"AUTHORISE — ERPNext-Production-Shell-Recipe-Drift-Fix-1"*) directed Cursor to correct the canonical production-shell recipe based on live execution reality captured in `JE-2026-06-04-5` (host_name fix closure on `corpflowai-production.localhost` on `corpflow-exec-01-u69678`). **Seven targeted corrections applied:** (1) Docker Compose project names corrected throughout the recipe from `erpnext-production` / `erpnext-sandbox` to `corpflowai-production` / `corpflowai-sandbox` — 35 `-p <project>` flag replacements + 8 prose / change-log replacements; filesystem directory paths `~/erpnext-production/` / `~/erpnext-sandbox/` and credential file paths `~/.erpnext-production-credentials` / `~/.erpnext-sandbox-credentials` deliberately kept unchanged because they match Anton's live filesystem (the directory naming was chosen at clone time and is decoupled from the Docker Compose project name, which is the operationally meaningful identifier on `docker compose ls`); a new explicit v1.1 alignment note in § 5 explains this distinction so future operators don't confuse the two; (2) § 5 production-port override hardened — replaced plain `ports: ["127.0.0.1:8081:8080"]` with `ports: !override [...]` Docker Compose v2 tag so the inline `compose.cf-production-port.yaml` override REPLACES the inherited `compose.noproxy.yaml` port binding instead of merely APPENDING (Compose v2 merges `ports:` lists across overlays by default, which would have left both the noproxy default `8080:8080` and the production `8081:8080` bindings live simultaneously and caused port-conflict / double-binding chaos); same `!override` tag also added for the socketio port `127.0.0.1:13001:9000` to avoid collision with the sandbox stack's `13000:9000`; (3) § 6 gains a new "(v1.1) PRE-FLIGHT: VERIFY DB ROOT PASSWORD IS WIRED CORRECTLY" step inserted before `bench new-site` — runs `mysql --user=root --password="$MARIADB_ROOT_PASSWORD" -e "SELECT 1 AS db_root_password_works\G"` from inside the `db` container and matches on `db_root_password_works` (the password value itself is never printed, only the success-marker string) — designed to catch the cascade of cryptic `mysql.connector.errors.OperationalError: Access denied` failures that result when `DB_PASSWORD` (env), `MARIADB_ROOT_PASSWORD` (env), `MYSQL_ROOT_PASSWORD` (compose), and `~/.erpnext-production-credentials` drift apart silently; § 6 "Expected output" section gains a corresponding v1.1 paragraph describing how to interpret the new check; (4) NEW § 7.5 "(v1.1) PDF rendering: set host_name and confirm wkhtmltopdf is unblocked" — adds the `bench --site corpflowai-production.localhost set-config host_name "http://frontend:8080"` step + `bench clear-cache` + minimal raw-HTML PDF smoke (via `frappe.utils.pdf.get_pdf()` against a 6-line inline HTML string with zero doctype dependencies, smallest possible blast radius) + `docker compose cp` of the PDF out to the host filesystem + optional `docker compose restart queue-short queue-long scheduler` for background-rendered PDFs; full causal-chain explanation of why the Docker DNS resolution of `frontend:8080` is required (backend container cannot resolve loopback hostname `corpflowai-production.localhost`; Docker DNS only knows Compose service names); cross-links to `JE-2026-06-04-5` (execution closure) + `ERPNEXT_PRINT_DESIGNER_EVALUATION_V1.md` § 3 *Diagnosis* + upstream `frappe/erpnext` Issue #36018 + `frappe/frappe_docker` Issue #1589; (5) NEW § 7.6 "(v1.1) Seed safeguards: Warehouse Type: Transit + default Mauritius Address Template" — idempotent Python orchestrator inside the existing backend container (zero new shell complexity) that uses `frappe.db.exists()` short-circuit guards to seed two ERPNext defaults that are usually but not always created by `bench install-app erpnext` on fresh v15 docker stacks; without them, § 8 Address creation and § 11 Item creation can fail with cryptic `LinkValidationError: Could not find Warehouse Type: Transit` / `LinkValidationError: Could not find Address Template: Mauritius`; the seed orchestrator prints `already_present` on every subsequent invocation and never duplicates rows; (6) § 16 v15 Quotation field corrected — `'remarks'` → `'customer_remarks'` in both the idempotency check (`frappe.db.get_value('Quotation', {..., 'remarks': ['like', f'%{TAG}%'], ...})`) and the doctype insert (`'remarks': f'TEST-ONLY PDF SMOKE — ...'`); closes the `pymysql.err.OperationalError: (1054, "Unknown column 'remarks' in 'SELECT'")` latent bug discovered during `JE-2026-06-04-5` Block A discovery; in-code comment cross-links the live-discovery evidence;
